3 years later and I've come to revisit this review. I personally owned what would have been considered to be the most beautifully trimmed Nismo 370Z. It was a nice platform and ear to ear smiles on the interstate and on the racetrack. Only needed an easily installed oil cooler to make things perfect. Unfortunately the new Z even with its twin turbo leaves too much to be desired for the price. Check out your local CarMax or carvana website and you will find the new Z in various forms readily available. The fun Factor was lost with this car, its styling and aesthetics and underwhelming horsepower makes it lackluster at best. The price point is ridiculous for what you're getting,  I can't explain it but Nissan's alcantara wears very quickly. I looked at a pre-owned version with only 4000 mi on it , the interior looked horrific, which was the same experience for myself and my NIsmo 370. Nissan has never been able to get this car exactly right, and unfortunately the new Z is another long-term disappointment. At about 56,000 + dollars for a low mi version, I go buy a  pre-owned 911 Porsche for 10k more. If I set every negative aside and this car had tons of horsepower to the rear wheel, to make it a thrilling Drive things would be different. Unfortunately you're always left short and wanting a little more.

I think the car is brilliant.  It's a love letter to drivers cars of the past.  No overly complicated electronics, manual parking brake, just a car that does what it needs to, and will likely be the darling of every tuning event of the next couple of years.  It is a classic sports car, that doesn't try to straddle the sports and luxury realms at the same time, which is smart, since Infiniti has the luxury bit covered.  Sure, there are recycled parts from older Nissan and Infiniti vehicles in this thing, but...they built the whole car themselves.  I think besides the automatic, the biggest turn-off for the Supra is that it's a BMW with Toyota badging (yes, I know there's more to them than that), and that will work in the Zed's favor. It will also have all of the aftermarket support from tuning and performance parts vendors that modded the 350 and 370 Zed, and those things will likely be a lot more affordable than the parts for the Supra, especially as it gets older.  Well done Nissan, now go and build an S-ER Spec V Sentra with a LSD and over 250hp, and you'll start drawing in the sport compact crowd again like you once did...

As somebody who used to hate multiple drive modes, cruise control and lane-assist, I am happy all those features came in my Veloster N.  Cruise control and lane keep assist were a huge help when i drove to Canada and occasionally needed to take my hands off the wheel or rest my feet. Jumping between regular mode and my custom performance mode is seamless and a huge help when I don't want to announce myself via tailpipes. Eco mode is pretty useless in the car though, the lower idle rpm makes it hard to engage the clutch and I'm not burning my clutch to same a few miles on my trip. Rev-matching works amazing but I'll always have it off unless I take it to the track. (rev-matching also doesn't work in eco mode where I need it most)  Hope I get to get my hands on this car and give it a ride, lord knows it's the only Nissan I would be caught dead in (minus the GTR of course). Putting the power port of to the side is freaking genius. Maybe it didn't need a guage but quickly being able to see your battery voltage without using a voltmeter or shuffling through menus is pretty damn cool too. I love to see features for real drivers going into these cars.

Bonus Fact: The new Z marks the first time since 1969 that the Z and Skyline/GT-R have shared an engine. In 1969, the Nissan Z (PS30) 432 (a variant of the 240Z) was powered by the Nissan S20 2.0L inline-6 (as opposed to its usual L20 inline-6). The S20 was originally used in the C10 and C110 Nissan Skylines. Now, in 2022, the Nissan VR-series Twin-Turbo V6 is included in the Z, Skyline (aka. Infiniti Q-car), and GT-R.

It cost something like $2,400, and is sold separately from the car. I feel that this is how they are attempting to make up a couple Grand of the cost off of the car, because they know everyone who buys the car is going to think to themselves "well I saved two or three thousand dollars not buying the Supra, so I can afford to buy the tuned exhaust." Then Nissan gets the amount for the car that they actually need to get for the car, which at that point would be closer to the cost of a supra. Respectfully I make a broad, sweeping statement regarding retro remakes: Mini, Mustang, VW beetle, Fiat 500, Land Rover defender, Suzuki Katana, etc. What is common to all of the original ICONS was simplicity in its technology but proficiency it what made it popular. It delivered the essentials - cost effective performance,(mustang), fuel efficiency with sufficient interior space(mini), robust hardwearing reliability, charm, a peoples car(VW beetle) and jeep like agricultural unapologetic functionality off road. Was there any real need to deviate from THOSE characteristics which popularised them in the first place. Research governing the tweaks have lead to a diluting of 'the essence' of most of these cars. By introducing advanced technology with generous market competitive interfaces & features, engine, transmission and ride adjustment settings, carry over parts from newer models etc, the redesigned nod to the original fails dismally. Basics with necessary technological improvements where it enhances the originals selling points, not detract from them. Does ANYONE REALLY need all those modern extras. They are missing the point. It makes me frustrated. To their credit, new corvette, Dodge demon, Ford GT40 know what they are doing. Big up to them. Thanks for reading...

I may be completely wrong, but I suspect this will be the final Z model for a decently long time.  The fact that they re used so much including the entire chassis from the 370z makes this essentially a very very intensive redesign, rather than a new platform. It's a mashup of a lot of pre-developed drivetrain and interior parts all put together with new sheet metal.   Also, the retro design combines a little of each generation, which may not mean much in itself, but it could signal no next generation/ clean sheet platform. Finally, I find it mildly interesting that they included the font on the rear window to say "since 1969 -" instead of just "since 1969."   I suspect they may be planning a top trim, limited edition farwell model in the future as a send off which may put a date after the hyphen in the "Since 1969 -" font.  Again, I could be wrong, but it wouldn't be a bad way to make a heritage based send-off with a cash-cow limited final edition, to possibly give way to the next generation hybrid/electric Nissan sports car.  We'll see.

A voltage gauge is far more important than you may realize.  It's typically one I add, especially in a limited use vehicle as you can see at a glance if the battery is topped off, and if the charging system is working properly.  Much more telling than a warning light.    Having it up and to the middle out of your immediate line of sight is also very handy.  Notice they have a boost gauge in the performance screen, as well as water/oil temperature, diff temp, and oil pressure.  All much more important "need to know right now" gauges, while the secondary boost gauge, turbine speed, and voltage are secondary but useful.  I'd also love for manufacturers to stop "including" navigation.  As long as you have car play/android auto, you have navigation.  It's also always up to date, and generally better.

I've owned 4 Z-cars, including a 2015 370z Sport 6MT. My only complaints about that car were 1) Lack of telescoping steering wheel and  2) Crappy stock seats. It looks like the "new" Z addresses those concerns, plus adds power and technology.  Here are my issues with this car:   This is a parts bin car. It's clearly a tweaked 370z with an engine swap to a powerplant Nissan/Infiniti has already made for several years. That would be fine, except that in order to get one with an LSD and Akebono brakes (carried over from the 370z), you pay $50k+, and that's not even including inevitable dealer mark-ups. For comparison- Less than 3 years ago, you could buy a brand new 370z Sport (LSD, Akebono brakes, 19 inch Rays wheels) for under $35k. Nissan has essentially raised the price of the equivalent "new" Z by $15k+ over the 370z, without building a new chassis. That's not good for consumers. They've priced this to compete with the Supra, disregarding the incredible value proposition this car could have been.  If we look at the base model, it's still $40k+. That might not seem bad, but it's still $10k more than what you could buy a base 370z for less than 3 years ago. It's also more than you can currently pay for a base Mustang GT or Camaro LT1. Even in the current inflated market, those cars are selling for under $40k in many parts of the country. You could buy a brand new 7th Gen Corvette for under $55k 2 or 3 years ago. As much as a love the Z, that's a better sports car. Even now there are used, low-mileage C7s out there for well under $50k.  I think this Z34.5 would be a home run if the base model started at $35k, and the performance trim topped out at $42-43k. I just don't think we're getting enough "new" sports car for the price.

As awesome as this car is shaping up to be, a new car with switches, stalks, e-brake, and modified door cards from a car that started production about 14 years ago is honestly... highly disappointing. It's a car with a starting price of $40k or so, and some of the parts in this car are old enough to start attending high school. Small things like this make such a nice looking car look cheap. While you won't be actively looking at them as often as you do the gauge cluster, shifter, and infotainment screen, it's frankly unacceptable. Nissan does a good job milking everything they can from their cars for too long, and the small details showing exactly that in a brand new performance car is annoying.
I think this car is for those who can actually drive and don't care about everything else yet needs a new car.

Clutch feel in older Z models was handicapped by a helper spring on the pedal arm/linkage.  I would not be surprised if there was one in the new car as well.  It's supposed to make the pedal easier to use, but it takes away the natural feedback you expect from a clutch pedal and gives a very nonlinear springy feel.  You end up feeling (and fighting) the spring rather than feeling the clutch and its engagement.  Apparently you can tear the spring out with some pliers (or replace it with a less aggressive spring) and greatly improve the feel, but why the heck couldn't Nissan get this right to begin with?  It's not like a clutch pedal is some newfangled technology...

Funny you should start this video with a Mk5 Supra, it looks a bit like a modern 240z with a body kit. Datsun originally took design elements from rival sports cars of the day (like the Alpha Romeo Spyder, Fiat Dino, Toyota 2000gt, Aston Martin DBS and the Jaguar E-Type). It seems car makers have been doing the same since the turn of the century with the original Z cars. Aston Martin made a few cars in the 00s (like the Vantage and DB9/10) that were similar looking. Jaguar also made the F-type which shares many similarities. More recently, Mercedes has the AMG GT and Ferrari has the Omologata, Roma, 812 superfast and the new BR20 that could all pass as Z car remakes. This new Z car looks more similar to the concept Z car Nissan made in the late 90s/ early 2000s. I think the Mazda Miata (or MX-5) has come closest to replicating the original Z cars in spirit - and the newest model could pass for a Z car as well!
